Conversation with Gemini

nothing shows

When you say "nothing shows," which part of the screen went blank on you? Depending on what you're looking at, it points to different things:
Scenario A: The Extension Popup is a Blank/White Box

If you click the toolbar icon and a small, empty, transparent or white rectangle opens up with zero content inside:

    The Cause: This is a classic frontend build failure in custom nightly forks. The HTML page (ui/popup/index.html) is loading, but the JavaScript bundle (React/Webpack) is throwing a silent compilation or mounting error before it can draw the UI.

    The Fix: Open your about:debugging extension console again, but this time click Inspect and switch to the Console tab while keeping that blank popup window open. It will usually spit out a red TypeError or ReferenceError indicating that a script file failed to load.

Scenario B: The Extension Console is Completely Empty

If you opened the hidden console via about:debugging and nothing prints when you click the button:

    The Cause: The background script is still completely asleep or crashed (Background script Stopped). Firefox isn't firing the event listener to trigger the popup.

    The Fix: In about:debugging, click the Reload button right next to the extension to force-kick the background service worker back into memory, then try clicking the extension icon again.

Scenario C: Running /opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge in Terminal outputs nothing

If you typed the path into your terminal and it just sits there on a blank line without returning to the prompt:

    The Cause: This is actually a good thing! The bridge uses stdio (standard input/output) to communicate. When it runs natively, it is supposed to sit there silently waiting for Firefox to feed it raw data packets. If it doesn't crash instantly, the binary itself is healthy.

Which one of these matches what you're seeing right now?

when clicking the fx_cast icon it doesnt open a window like usual

Now that the security block is completely out of the way, Firefox is finally attempting to execute the initialization script. If the window isn't opening, the click handler is getting stuck on a pending promise—likely because the bridge process is launching but failing its initialization handshake.

Let's find out exactly where the thread is hanging with two quick checks.
1. Check if the Process is Spawning (and Staying Alive)

When you click that icon, Firefox should instantly fork a background process for the bridge. Let's see if it's actually running or if it's crashing immediately.

    Keep Firefox open.

    Click the fx_cast icon.

    Open a terminal and immediately run:
    Bash

    ps aux | grep fx_cast_bridge

    If you see a running process path matching /opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge: The binary is alive but hanging. It might be waiting indefinitely for local network discovery (mDNS) or an explicit response schema.

    If you see nothing but your own grep command: The binary is crashing the millisecond Firefox spawns it.

2. Grab the New Click-Event Error Log

Since the extension ID is now verified, the previous error messages are out of date. Let's see what the background script says the exact moment you trigger the click event.

    Go back to about:debugging#/runtime/this-firefox.

    Click Inspect next to fx_cast-nightly@gitxpresso to open the extension console.

    Click the Clear Console trash bin icon at the top left of that inspector window so it's completely blank.

    Go back to your main browser window and click the fx_cast toolbar icon.

Does a fresh error drop into the console right when you click it? If so, what does it say? (Look for terms like Error: An unexpected error occurred, JSON.parse, or Bridge disconnected).

nvm it works but i can click the arrows or do anything to cast

The good news is that your communication channel is now 100% functional. The fact that your actual device names ("Bedroom display", "Guest Bedroom", and "room5") are appearing means the extension successfully spawned your nightly bridge binary, and the bridge scanned your local network and fed the list back to the browser perfectly.

The bad news is that you've run straight into a JavaScript execution crash inside the extension's frontend interface.
Why the Arrows Aren't Responding

Look at the red error at the bottom of your inspector window:

    Uncaught (in promise) Error: Invalid window ID: 167

This is a deep-seated compatibility bug in the extension's code. When you click the toolbar icon, the extension opens its popup panel and tries to query Firefox for the ID of the active browser window to determine what tab you want to cast.

In newer Firefox versions, the way extension popup panels are handled isolates their window IDs differently. The extension is passing a stale or forbidden window reference (167), which causes Firefox's internal API (ExtensionCommon.sys.mjs) to throw an uncaught promise rejection. The moment that happens, the entire JavaScript state machine running the popup dies, which instantly freezes all click listeners on those rows and dropdown arrows.
How to Bypass the Broken Popup

Since the toolbar popup UI is crashing on window matching, you have to bypass it entirely. Fortunately, fx_cast is designed to inject Google's Cast API directly into webpages so you don't have to use the toolbar icon.

Try these two alternate casting paths:
1. Use the Video Player's Native Cast Button (Most Reliable)

    Go to the extension's settings/options page and ensure the site you want to use (like YouTube) is allowed in the Site Whitelist.

    Open a video on that site.

    Instead of clicking the Firefox toolbar icon, look at the video player control bar (next to the volume/fullscreen settings) and click the native casting icon inside the video player itself.

    This invokes the casting API directly from the tab's context, avoiding the broken popup window code path.

2. Use the Right-Click Context Menu

    Right-click an empty area on the webpage you want to stream.

    Look for a Cast... option added by the extension in your browser's right-click context menu.

    Triggering it from the page context sometimes circumvents the panel tracking logic and routes the media stream directly to the bridge.

Are you getting the same Invalid window ID failure when you attempt to cast from the player's native button on a whitelisted site?

how to fix the broken UI?

To fix this broken UI, you need to patch a classic Firefox WebExtension architectural bug in your local fx_cast source code, recompile it, and reload it.
Why This is Happening (The Technical Cause)

The error Invalid window ID: 167 happens because of how Firefox isolates extension popup panels.

When you click the extension icon, the popup opens. If the underlying code calls browser.windows.getCurrent() or queries tabs using { currentWindow: true }, Firefox often returns the window ID of the popup panel container itself instead of the main browser window behind it. The moment you move your mouse or interact with it, that panel context shifts or closes, rendering that window ID completely dead. When the background script tries to process the bridge's device list using that stale ID, the JavaScript state engine crashes, freezing the UI.

Since you are running a custom nightly fork (fx_cast-nightly@gitxpresso), you can fix this directly in the source files.
Step 1: Locate the Offending Window Logic

Open a terminal in your local fx_cast source repository and search for where the extension fetches the active window or tab IDs.

Run grep or ripgrep to find the culprit:
Bash

grep -rn "windows.getCurrent" src/
# or check tab queries matching the active window
grep -rn "currentWindow:" src/

You are looking for lines in the extension frontend/background code (likely under src/extension/ or src/background/) that look like this:
JavaScript

browser.windows.getCurrent()
// or
browser.tabs.query({ active: true, currentWindow: true })

Step 2: Apply the Patch

To prevent Firefox from grabbing the transient popup window ID, you must explicitly tell it to target the last focused normal browser window.
Fix Type A: If it's a Window query

Change getCurrent() to target only normal browser windows:
JavaScript

// BEFORE
const currentWindow = await browser.windows.getCurrent();

// AFTER
const currentWindow = await browser.windows.getLastFocused({ windowTypes: ["normal"] });

Fix Type B: If it's a Tab query

If the crash is happening inside a tabs.query block, swap currentWindow out for lastFocusedWindow:
JavaScript

// BEFORE
const [tab] = await browser.tabs.query({ active: true, currentWindow: true });

// AFTER
const [tab] = await browser.tabs.query({ active: true, lastFocusedWindow: true });

Step 3: Recompile and Refresh

Once you've swapped those lines out to use the robust focused-window APIs:

    Rebuild the extension files in your terminal:
    Bash

    npm run build:extension
    # or whatever build/package command your specific fork uses

    Go back to Firefox and navigate to about:debugging#/runtime/this-firefox.

    Find your fx_cast-nightly@gitxpresso extension and click the Reload button.

This will force the background script to clear its state and reload your updated window-matching logic. When you click the toolbar icon now, the clicks and dropdown arrows should register perfectly without throwing unhandled promise rejections!

src/ui/popup/Popup.svelte:118:        browserWindow = await browser.windows.getCurrent();

Perfect hit! Those are exactly the two lines freezing your UI. Both of them are trying to grab the "current" window, but in newer Firefox versions, that returns the transient popup window container itself rather than the actual browser window.

Open up your favorite editor and make these quick swaps:
1. Patch the Background Script

Open src/background/receiverSelector.ts and navigate to line 118.

Change this:
TypeScript

const refWin = await browser.windows.getCurrent();

To this:
TypeScript

const refWin = await browser.windows.getLastFocused({ windowTypes: ["normal"] });

2. Patch the Popup UI

Open src/ui/popup/Popup.svelte and navigate to line 118.

Change this:
TypeScript

browserWindow = await browser.windows.getCurrent();

To this:
TypeScript

browserWindow = await browser.windows.getLastFocused({ windowTypes: ["normal"] });

3. Rebuild and Re-evaluate

Now that you've forced Firefox to look past the extension's popup and target your actual main browser window, compile your extension changes:
Bash

npm run build:extension

(If your specific nightly structure packages everything at the root, a plain npm run build works too).

Once the build finishes:

    Return to about:debugging#/runtime/this-firefox.

    Find fx_cast-nightly@gitxpresso and click Reload.

    Fire up the toolbar icon and try clicking a receiver device.

The state engine shouldn't crash anymore, and those dropdown arrows/click bindings will be fully alive! Let me know if it successfully launches the stream.

allow unsigned xpi firefox

On standard Firefox Release or Beta builds, Mozilla explicitly locks down the ability to install unsigned .xpi files. Changing the signature requirement flag in about:config will be completely ignored by design.

To load your modified extension build, choose the method that fits your workflow:
Method 1: The Temporary Fix (Any Firefox Edition)

If you are actively developing or testing code changes and don't mind the extension unloading when you close the browser:

    Go to about:debugging#/runtime/this-firefox.

    Click Load Temporary Add-on...

    Select your .xpi file (or target the compiled manifest.json inside your build folder).

Method 2: The Permanent Fix (Requires Dev Edition, Nightly, or ESR)

To install unsigned .xpi files permanently without them vanishing on restart, you must use a build of Firefox that permits bypassing the check (Developer Edition, Nightly, or ESR).

    Open your advanced configuration editor by navigating to about:config.

    Accept the warning dialog.

    Search for: xpinstall.signatures.required

    Toggle the value from true to false.

    Open about:addons, click the gear icon at the top right, select Install Add-on From File..., and choose your .xpi.

Method 3: The Production Fix (Self-Signing for Standard Release)

If you want to keep using standard Firefox Release but want your custom build to remain permanently installed, you can use Mozilla’s automated pipeline to generate a personal digital signature. It won't be listed publicly on AMO.

    Grab a free API Key and Secret from the Mozilla Add-on Developer Hub.

    Navigate to your extension build directory and run the signing tool via npx:
    Bash

    npx web-ext sign --api-key="YOUR_JWT_ISSUER_KEY" --api-secret="YOUR_JWT_SECRET"

    Once the validation checks pass, grab the freshly signed .xpi from the newly created web-ext-artifacts/ folder.

Standard Firefox will now install this file normally through about:addons and let it run permanently.

Mozilla's signing server has a photographic memory. Once a specific version number (like 0.4.2) has been uploaded and processed under your extension ID, the server permanently locks it. Even if you've modified the code locally, you cannot overwrite an existing version on their system, resulting in that 409 Conflict error.

To get your patched build signed, you just need to bump the version number.
1. Update the Version Number

Open the manifest.json file inside your source directory:
Bash

nano /home/gitxpresso/Downloads/fx_cast/extension/src/manifest.json

Look for the "version" field near the top of the file:
JSON

"version": "0.4.2",

Change it to an unused incremental version, such as:
JSON

"version": "0.4.3",

(Alternatively, you can use a revision string like "0.4.2.1" if you want to keep track of your local patches).

Save the file (Ctrl+O, then Ctrl+X).
2. Run the Sign Command Again

Execute your signing script or command again from the terminal:
Bash

nsign --channel unlisted

The server will see 0.4.3 as a completely fresh update, pass it through the automated verification pipeline, and successfully drop your freshly signed, UI-fixed .xpi file into your artifacts folder.

The automated linter at Mozilla rejected the upload because it's looking at raw code rather than a compiled browser extension.

Look closely at this line in your terminal output:

    Building web extension from /home/gitxpresso/Downloads/fx_cast/extension/src

Because fx_cast relies on TypeScript (.ts) and Svelte (.svelte), you cannot sign the raw src/ folder. Mozilla's validator expects standard browser-ready vanilla JavaScript, HTML, and CSS. When it scans your src/ directory and finds uncompiled source files, it instantly triggers a fatal validation failure.

You need to compile the project first and point your signing tool to the build output directory.
1. Run the Build Step

Ensure your latest window-matching patches are compiled down to vanilla assets. Run this from the extension/ root directory:
Bash

npm run build

(Depending on the fork's configuration, this command might be npm run build:extension or npm run package).
2. Locate the Output Folder

Once the build completes, a new directory containing the distribution assets will be generated. In the fx_cast project structure, this is typically a folder named dist/ or build/ located inside the extension/ directory.

Verify it contains a compiled manifest.json along with flat .js and .html bundles (no .ts or .svelte files).
3. Sign the Compiled Output Directory

Now, run your signing command again, but explicitly pass the path to that compiled folder using the --source-dir (or -s) flag.

If the output folder is named dist, run:
Bash

web-ext sign --channel unlisted --source-dir ./dist

If your custom nsign alias doesn't accept trailing path arguments easily, simply change your working directory into that compiled folder first and run it from there:
Bash

cd dist
nsign --channel unlisted

Mozilla's server will validate the clean production assets, approve the file, and drop your signed, fully-functional .xpi file right into the web-ext-artifacts/ directory.

It looks like the screencast shows the next hurdle after trying to compile or load the patched extension.

Depending on which stage of the video you are looking at, here is how to resolve the common issues that pop up right after applying this patch:
1. If the video shows a build error in the terminal (npm run build failed)

If TypeScript or Svelte choked when you tried to compile, it’s usually due to a strict type mismatch with the new getLastFocused method.

    The Culprit: browser.windows.getLastFocused() returns a Windows.Window object, but the original code might be expecting a specific structure or wrapper.

    The Quick Fix: Cast the type or change how it assigns the window ID. For example, if it's complaining about types in src/background/receiverSelector.ts, you can look at what property it accesses next (like refWin.id). Ensure it handles the fact that id might technically be optional/undefined in the types:
    TypeScript

    const refWin = await browser.windows.getLastFocused({ windowTypes: ["normal"] });
    const windowId = refWin?.id;

2. If the video shows the UI opening but clicking a device still does nothing

If the popup opens, shows your devices (Bedroom display, room5, etc.), but clicking them still results in a freeze without the Invalid window ID error:

    Check the Console: Open the about:debugging inspector console again. Look for a brand new error message.

    The Common Next Culprit: The extension might be failing to match the current tab URL to an allowed mirroring format, or the bridge binary (/opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge) might be dropping the connection when the actual casting stream initializes.

    To test if it's a packaging issue: Instead of signing it permanently right away, click Load Temporary Add-on in about:debugging and point it directly to the built manifest.json inside your compiled dist/ or build/ folder. If the temporary version works perfectly, then the issue is entirely down to the web-ext sign packaging loop.

3. If the video shows web-ext sign still failing on the output folder

If you ran web-ext sign --source-dir ./dist (or your alias) and it still failed validation:

    Check the generated validation URL provided in the terminal output. It will tell you the exact file causing the rejection.

    Sometimes, build tools copy over files like manifest.json.bak, markdown documentation, or hidden .git structures into the build folder, which the Mozilla linter flags as invalid assets. Deleting those extra files out of the output folder before signing will clean up the build.

help me fix the extension with an advanced python script

Since your screencast shows you already successfully patched the window IDs in vim, rebuilt the .zip, and got the UI to physically render your devices, the extension's rendering engine is now fully operational.

If clicking a device still does absolutely nothing to initiate a cast, you are hitting the hardest part of WebExtension debugging: the "invisible wall" between Firefox and the native Linux system. Either the extension UI click-handler is failing to send the "start cast" payload, or the bridge binary is receiving the payload and silently crashing.

To fix this, we need an advanced Python proxy script. We are going to replace your bridge binary with a "Wiretap" script. This script will sit directly between Firefox and the fx_cast binary, intercept the proprietary native-messaging protocol in real-time, log every single JSON packet going back and forth to a text file, and then seamlessly forward the traffic so the extension still thinks it's talking to the real backend.
1. Set Up the Python Wiretap

First, rename your existing, real binary so we can safely wrap it:
Bash

sudo mv /opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge /opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge.real

Now, create the Python script in its place:
Bash

sudo nano /opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge

Paste this robust native-messaging interceptor into the file:
Python

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import sys
import struct
import subprocess
import threading
import json

REAL_BRIDGE = "/opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge.real"
LOG_FILE = "/tmp/fx_cast_debug.log"

def log(msg):
    try:
        with open(LOG_FILE, "a") as f:
            f.write(msg + "\n")
    except:
        pass

def forward(src, dst, direction):
    while True:
        try:
            # The native messaging protocol sends a 32-bit integer header for the message length
            raw_len = src.read(4)
            if not raw_len or len(raw_len) < 4:
                break
            
            msg_len = struct.unpack('@I', raw_len)[0]
            
            # Read the actual JSON payload based on the header length
            msg_bytes = src.read(msg_len)
            parsed_json = json.loads(msg_bytes.decode('utf-8'))
            
            # Log the beautifully formatted JSON packet
            log(f"[{direction}]\n{json.dumps(parsed_json, indent=2)}\n")
            
            # Forward the exact raw bytes to the destination
            dst.write(raw_len)
            dst.write(msg_bytes)
            dst.flush()
        except Exception as e:
            log(f"[{direction} ERROR] {str(e)}")
            break

def main():
    log("=== NEW CAST SESSION INITIATED ===")
    
    # Spawn the real bridge daemon in the background
    proc = subprocess.Popen(
        [REAL_BRIDGE],
        stdin=subprocess.PIPE,
        stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
        stderr=subprocess.PIPE
    )
    
    # Thread 1: Listen to Firefox (sys.stdin) -> Forward to Bridge (proc.stdin)
    t1 = threading.Thread(
        target=forward, 
        args=(sys.stdin.buffer, proc.stdin, "FIREFOX -> BRIDGE"),
        daemon=True
    )
    t1.start()
    
    # Main Thread: Listen to Bridge (proc.stdout) -> Forward to Firefox (sys.stdout)
    forward(proc.stdout, sys.stdout.buffer, "BRIDGE -> FIREFOX")
    
    proc.wait()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

2. Lock It In and Execute

Make the Python script executable so Firefox is allowed to run it:
Bash

sudo chmod +x /opt/fx_cast/fx_cast_bridge

The log confirms your bridge binary is working perfectly and communicating with your devices. However, the logs reveal the two critical points of failure that are preventing the cast from launching:
1. The manifest.json Security Lockdown

The error ‘script-src’ directive contains a forbidden 'unsafe-eval' keyword is the primary reason the UI click-handlers are failing.

Firefox's modern Manifest V3 security policy strictly forbids unsafe-eval. When the extension tries to evaluate the callback functions attached to your device buttons, the browser intercepts the "unsafe" execution and kills the script.

The Fix:
Open your src/manifest.json and locate the content_security_policy block. You must remove unsafe-eval and replace it with a hash or simply remove the directive if the extension is built to be modern.

    Remove: 'unsafe-eval'

    Add (if necessary): 'self' or blob: depending on how the Svelte components are bundled.

2. The Logic Silence (The "Invisible Wall")

Look at your wiretap log again. Notice that after the discovery phase finishes:
JSON

[BRIDGE -> FIREFOX]
{ "subject": "main:receiverDeviceStatusUpdated", ... }

...there is zero [FIREFOX -> BRIDGE] output when you click a device.

This confirms that the UI event listener is not even firing. Because of the security error above, the click event is being blocked by Firefox's CSP, so the command to "launch the app" (bridge:launchApp) is never sent to the bridge.
How to resolve this entirely

You have a "Security versus Functionality" mismatch. Here is the path to finish this:
Step A: Relax the Security (Temporary Development)

To prove this is the fix, go to about:config, search for extensions.manifestV3.enabled, and make sure it is set to true. Then, in your manifest.json, strip the content_security_policy entirely for a moment. This will bypass the "unsafe-eval" error. Rebuild, reload the extension, and click a device. If it works, you know exactly where the blocking is.
Step B: The "Svelte-Friendly" Fix

If you want to keep the security policies, you must change how your Svelte components interact with the background script.

    Move logic to the background script: Do not execute logic inside the popup UI (Popup.svelte).

    Use Message Passing: Have Popup.svelte send a simple browser.runtime.sendMessage({ action: 'CAST', deviceId: '...' }) to a background worker script.

    Handle in Background: Have background/index.ts perform the bridge:launchApp call.

Because the background script has different security permissions than the popup UI, it won't be blocked by the script-src directive that's currently stopping your clicks.

Are you ready to move the click-logic to the background script to bypass the CSP block, or would you like to try to weaken the CSP first to confirm that the click-logic works once unblocked?

provide me files to send you

The manifest.json you provided shows that your extension is currently running in Manifest V3 mode without a defined content_security_policy.

In Firefox MV3, if you don't define a policy, it defaults to a very strict one that prohibits unsafe-eval, inline scripts, and remote resources. Because your extension uses Svelte (which relies heavily on dynamic DOM manipulation and often pre-compilation-in-memory techniques that modern browsers interpret as "eval"-like behavior), this strict default is likely what is killing your UI click-handlers.

To resolve the "Forbidden 'unsafe-eval'" error and get the UI buttons to function, you need to explicitly define a policy that allows the extension to function.
The Fix: Update your manifest.json

Add the content_security_policy block to your manifest.json. You should place this at the same level as manifest_version or background.
JSON

    "manifest_version": 3,
    "content_security_policy": {
        "extension_pages": "script-src 'self'; object-src 'self';"
    },
    "options_ui": {
        "page": "ui/options/index.html"
    },

Wait! If adding that specific line still results in an error, it means your Svelte-compiled code is genuinely trying to run eval() or a similar function directly. Since unsafe-eval is forbidden in MV3, you have two options to proceed:

    The "Hard" Fix (The correct long-term way): You must re-compile your Svelte code without the "runtime compiler." If you are using a build system (like vite or rollup), ensure your Svelte plugin is set to use the "runtime-only" or "precompiled" mode. This moves the logic from "compiling on the fly" to "pre-calculated code," which MV3 is perfectly happy with.

    The "Quick" Fix (For testing): Temporarily revert to Manifest V2. Change "manifest_version": 3 to "manifest_version": 2 in your manifest.json. V2 is much more lenient and will allow your existing Svelte code to run exactly as it is without security-related crashes.

    src/ui/popup/Popup.svelte (or whichever file handles the device list click event).

    src/background/background.js (to see how the nativeMessaging port is opened and how it handles messages).

    src/background/receiverSelector.js (or the file responsible for triggering the bridge:launchApp command).

This is a comprehensive look at your fx_cast source. Because you've confirmed that the Wiretap shows no [FIREFOX -> BRIDGE] output when you click a receiver, we know the "Launch Command" is dying somewhere in the Message Chain.

To fix this, we need to trace that chain from the UI to the system bridge. Please provide the content of the following 4 files. You can cat/output them here one by one, or paste their contents:
1. src/ui/popup/Popup.svelte (The Trigger)

This is where we need to verify that your click handler is actually executing and finding the correct deviceId. If the click event isn't triggering the messaging function, the chain breaks here.
2. src/background/castManager.ts (The Orchestrator)

This is the most critical file. It should contain the logic that receives the request from the popup and decides to call the bridge. I need to see if your castManager has a method to handle the "Launch App" request.
3. src/lib/bridge.ts (The Transport)

This is the low-level wrapper around the native messaging port. If the castManager is correctly sending the command, this file might be failing to serialize or dispatch the data to the Python/Native binary.
4. src/background/background.ts (The Listener)

I need to verify that your background script is correctly setting up the runtime.onMessage listener to catch the request from the popup and forward it to the castManager.
Why these 4 files?

We are looking for the "Silent Failure." The chain looks like this:

Popup.svelte (Click) → browser.runtime.sendMessage → background.ts (Listener) → castManager.ts (Logic) → bridge.ts (Send to Native) → Wiretap

If you paste the content of these files, I can pinpoint exactly which step is failing to forward the signal. Please paste the content of the first file, and I will guide you through the check.

provide me a one liner to copy all contents of each file

To grab the contents of all your relevant source files and put them directly onto your clipboard (so you can paste them here in one go), run this command from the fx_cast/extension directory:
Bash

find src/ -type f \( -name "*.ts" -o -name "*.svelte" \) -exec echo -e "\n\n--- FILE: {} ---" \; -exec cat {} \; | xclip -selection clipboard

Why this is the best way:

    find src/: It only looks at your source code, ignoring binary icons, images, and build artifacts.

    \( -name "*.ts" -o -name "*.svelte" \): It filters specifically for your TypeScript and Svelte files.

    echo -e "\n\n--- FILE: {} ---": It inserts the filename as a header before every file, which is critical for me to understand the context of the code.

    xclip: This dumps the result directly into your system clipboard.

Note: If you get a "command not found" for xclip, you can install it via sudo dnf install xclip. If you prefer to save it to a file instead of the clipboard, just replace | xclip -selection clipboard with > all_code.txt.

Once you run that, just Paste (Ctrl+V) the result into the chat. If the output is massive, feel free to just paste the content of the 4 specific files I requested (Popup.svelte, castManager.ts, bridge.ts, and background.ts) one by one.



--- FILE: src/background/action.ts ---

import logger from "../lib/logger";

import castManager from "./castManager";


const _ = browser.i18n.getMessage;


const ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_DARK = "icons/cast-default-dark.svg";

const ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_LIGHT = "icons/cast-default-light.svg";

const ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_DARK = "icons/cast-connecting-dark.svg";

const ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_LIGHT = "icons/cast-connecting-light.svg";

const ACTION_ICON_CONNECTED = "icons/cast-connected.svg";


const isDarkTheme = window.matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)").matches;


export enum ActionState {

    Default,

    Connecting,

    Connected

}


/** Updates action details depending on given state. */

export function updateActionState(state: ActionState, tabId?: number) {

    let title: string;

    let path = isDarkTheme

        ? ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_LIGHT

        : ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_DARK;


    switch (state) {

        case ActionState.Default:

            title = _("actionTitleDefault");

            break;

        case ActionState.Connecting:

            title = _("actionTitleConnecting");

            path = isDarkTheme

                ? ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_LIGHT

                : ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_DARK;

            break;

        case ActionState.Connected:

            title = _("actionTitleConnected");

            path = ACTION_ICON_CONNECTED;

            break;

    }


    browser.action.setTitle({ tabId, title });

    browser.action.setIcon({ tabId, path });

}


export function initAction() {

    logger.info("init (action)");


    updateActionState(ActionState.Default);


    browser.action.onClicked.addListener(async tab => {

        if (tab.id === undefined) {

            logger.error("Tab ID not found in browser action handler.");

            return;

        }


        castManager.triggerCast(tab.id);

    });

}



--- FILE: src/background/background.ts ---

import logger from "../lib/logger";

import options from "../lib/options";

import bridge, { type BridgeInfo } from "../lib/bridge";

import { baseConfigStorage, fetchBaseConfig } from "../lib/chromecastConfigApi";


import defaultOptions from "../defaultOptions";

import messaging from "../messaging";


import castManager from "./castManager";

import deviceManager from "./deviceManager";


import { initAction } from "./action";

import { initMenus } from "./menus";

import { initWhitelist } from "./whitelist";

import { cacheUaInfo, getChromeUserAgentString } from "../lib/userAgents";


const _ = browser.i18n.getMessage;


/**

 * On install, set the default options before initializing the

 * extension. On update, handle any unset values and set to the new

 * defaults.

 */

browser.runtime.onInstalled.addListener(async details => {

    switch (details.reason) {

        case "install": {

            // Set defaults

            await options.setAll(defaultOptions);


            // Extension initialization

            init();

            break;

        }


        case "update": {

            // Set new defaults

            await options.update(defaultOptions);

            break;

        }

    }

});


/**

 * Checks whether the bridge can be reached and is compatible with the

 * current version of the extension. If not, triggers a notification

 * with the appropriate info.

 */

async function notifyBridgeCompat() {

    logger.info("checking for bridge...");


    let info: BridgeInfo;

    try {

        info = await bridge.getInfo();

    } catch (err) {

        logger.info("... bridge issue!");

        return;

    }


    if (info.isVersionCompatible) {

        logger.info("... bridge compatible!");

    } else {

        logger.info("... bridge incompatible!");


        const updateNotificationId = await browser.notifications.create({

            type: "basic",

            title: `${_("extensionName")} — ${_(

                "optionsBridgeIssueStatusTitle"

            )}`,

            message: info.isVersionOlder

                ? _("optionsBridgeOlderAction")

                : _("optionsBridgeNewerAction")

        });


        browser.notifications.onClicked.addListener(notificationId => {

            if (notificationId !== updateNotificationId) {

                return;

            }


            browser.tabs.create({

                url: `https://github.com/hensm/fx_cast/releases/tag/v${info.expectedVersion}`

            });

        });

    }

}


/**

 * Updates locally-stored base config data if never downloaded or since

 * expired.

 */

async function cacheBaseConfig() {

    const { baseConfigUpdated } = await baseConfigStorage.get(

        "baseConfigUpdated"

    );


    // If never updated or updated more than 48 hours ago

    if (

        !baseConfigUpdated ||

        (Date.now() - baseConfigUpdated) / 1000 >= 172800

    ) {

        logger.info("Fetching updated Chromecast base config...");

        const baseConfig = await fetchBaseConfig();

        if (baseConfig) {

            await baseConfigStorage.set({

                baseConfig,

                baseConfigUpdated: Date.now()

            });

        }

    }

}


let isInitialized = false;


async function init() {

    if (isInitialized) {

        return;

    }


    /**

     * If options haven't been set yet, we can't properly initialize,

     * so wait until init is called again in the onInstalled listener.

     */

    if (!(await options.getAll())) {

        return;

    }


    logger.info("init");

    isInitialized = true;


    await notifyBridgeCompat();


    await deviceManager.init();

    await castManager.init();


    await initAction();

    await initMenus();

    await initWhitelist();


    messaging.onMessage.addListener(message => {

        switch (message.subject) {

            case "main:refreshDeviceManager":

                deviceManager.refresh();

                break;

        }

    });

}


cacheUaInfo();

cacheBaseConfig();

init();

import bridge from "../lib/bridge";

import {

    type BaseConfig,

    baseConfigStorage,

    getAppTag

} from "../lib/chromecastConfigApi";

import logger from "../lib/logger";

import messaging, { type Message, type Port } from "../messaging";

import options from "../lib/options";

import type { TypedMessagePort } from "../lib/TypedMessagePort";


import {

    type ReceiverDevice,

    type ReceiverSelectorAppInfo,

    ReceiverSelectorMediaType,

    type ReceiverSelectorPageInfo

} from "../types";


import type { ApiConfig } from "../cast/sdk/classes";

import { AutoJoinPolicy, ReceiverAction } from "../cast/sdk/enums";

import { createReceiver } from "../cast/utils";


import ReceiverSelector, {

    type ReceiverSelection,

    type ReceiverSelectorMediaMessage,

    type ReceiverSelectorReceiverMessage

} from "./receiverSelector";


import deviceManager from "./deviceManager";

import { ActionState, updateActionState } from "./action";


type AnyPort = Port | TypedMessagePort<Message>;


export interface ContentContext {

    tabId: number;

    frameId: number;

    origin?: string;

}


/** Checks if two content contexts match. */

function isSameContext(ctx1?: ContentContext, ctx2?: ContentContext) {

    if (!ctx1 || !ctx2) return false;

    return ctx1?.tabId === ctx2?.tabId && ctx1?.frameId === ctx2?.frameId;

}


interface CastSession {

    bridgePort: Port;

    deviceId: string;

    appId: string;

    sessionId?: string;

    autoJoinContexts: Set<ContentContext>;

}


/** Creates a cast session object and sets up messaging. */

async function createCastSession(opts: {

    deviceId: string;

    instance: CastInstance;

    appId?: string;

}) {

    // If not explicitly provided, use session request app ID

    if (!opts.appId) {

        if (!opts.instance.apiConfig?.sessionRequest) {

            throw logger.error(

                "App ID not provided and instance missing valid session request!"

            );

        }

        opts.appId = opts.instance.apiConfig.sessionRequest.appId;

    }


    const session: CastSession = {

        bridgePort: await bridge.connect(),

        deviceId: opts.deviceId,

        appId: opts.appId,

        autoJoinContexts: new Set()

    };


    if (opts.instance.contentContext) {

        session.autoJoinContexts.add(opts.instance.contentContext);

    }


    opts.instance.session = session;

    opts.instance.bridgeMessageListener = message => {

        handleBridgeMessage(opts.instance, message);

    };


    session.bridgePort.onMessage.addListener(

        opts.instance.bridgeMessageListener

    );

    session.bridgePort.onDisconnect.addListener(() =>

        destroyCastInstance(opts.instance)

    );


    if (opts.instance.contentContext?.tabId) {

        updateActionState(

            ActionState.Connecting,

            opts.instance.contentContext?.tabId

        );

    }


    return session;

}


function joinSession(instance: CastInstance, session: CastSession) {

    if (!session.sessionId) return;


    instance.session = session;

    instance.bridgeMessageListener = message =>

        handleBridgeMessage(instance, message);


    session.bridgePort.onMessage.addListener(instance.bridgeMessageListener);

    session.bridgePort.onDisconnect.addListener(() =>

        destroyCastInstance(instance)

    );


    const device = deviceManager.getDeviceById(session.deviceId);

    if (!device?.status?.applications?.length) {

        throw logger.error("Invalid device state!");

    }


    /**

     * Re-create sessionCreated message. Since the

     * sender app hasn't requested a session, this

     * will be handled by calling the session

     * listener.

     */

    const application = device?.status?.applications[0];

    instance.contentPort.postMessage({

        subject: "cast:sessionCreated",

        data: {

            appId: application.appId,

            appImages: [],

            displayName: application.displayName,

            namespaces: application.namespaces,

            receiverFriendlyName: device.friendlyName,

            receiverId: device.id,

            senderApps: [],

            sessionId: session.sessionId,

            statusText: application.statusText,

            transportId: session.sessionId,

            volume: device.status.volume,


            receiver: createReceiver(device),

            media: device.mediaStatus

        }

    });


    if (instance.contentContext?.tabId) {

        updateActionState(

            ActionState.Connected,

            instance.contentContext?.tabId

        );

    }

}


function leaveSession(instance: CastInstance) {

    if (!instance.session?.sessionId) return;


    instance.contentPort.postMessage({

        subject: "cast:sessionDisconnected",

        data: { sessionId: instance.session.sessionId }

    });


    delete instance.session;

    if (instance.contentContext?.tabId) {

        updateActionState(ActionState.Default, instance.contentContext.tabId);

    }

}


export interface CastInstance {

    contentPort: AnyPort;

    contentContext?: ContentContext;


    /** From an extension-source, grants additional permissions. */

    isTrusted: boolean;


    /** ApiConfig provided on initialization. */

    apiConfig?: ApiConfig;

    /** Established session details. */

    session?: CastSession;


    /** Listener for bridge messages. */

    bridgeMessageListener?: (message: Message) => void;

}


/** Creates a cast instance object and associated bridge instance. */

function createCastInstance(opts: {

    contentPort: AnyPort;

    contentContext?: { tabId: number; frameId?: number };

    isTrusted?: boolean;

}) {

    const instance: CastInstance = {

        contentPort: opts.contentPort,

        isTrusted: opts.isTrusted ?? false

    };


    /**

     * Set content context with fallback to extension message sender

     * context for content scripts.

     */

    if (opts.contentContext) {

        instance.contentContext = {

            tabId: opts.contentContext.tabId,

            frameId: opts.contentContext.frameId ?? 0

        };

    } else if (

        !(opts.contentPort instanceof MessagePort) &&

        opts.contentPort.sender?.tab?.id

    ) {

        // Get origin from content port

        let origin: Optional<string>;

        if (opts.contentPort.sender?.tab?.url) {

            try {

                ({ origin } = new URL(opts.contentPort.sender.tab.url));

                // eslint-disable-next-line no-empty

            } catch {}

        }


        instance.contentContext = {

            tabId: opts.contentPort.sender.tab.id,

            frameId: opts.contentPort.sender.frameId ?? 0,

            origin

        };

    }


    return instance;

}


/** Removes cast instance and disconnects messaging ports. */

function destroyCastInstance(instance: CastInstance) {

    if (instance.contentPort instanceof MessagePort) {

        instance.contentPort.close();

    } else {

        instance.contentPort.disconnect();

    }


    if (instance.session && instance.bridgeMessageListener) {

        instance.session.bridgePort.onMessage.removeListener(

            instance.bridgeMessageListener

        );

    }


    if (instance.contentContext?.tabId) {

        updateActionState(ActionState.Default, instance.contentContext?.tabId);

    }


    activeInstances.delete(instance);

}


/**

 * Check instance's auto join policy against a content context to

 * determine if it's a valid auto join target.

 */

function isValidAutoJoinContext(

    instance: CastInstance,

    context: ContentContext

) {

    if (!instance.apiConfig?.autoJoinPolicy) return false;


    const { autoJoinPolicy } = instance.apiConfig;

    if (

        autoJoinPolicy === AutoJoinPolicy.ORIGIN_SCOPED ||

        autoJoinPolicy === AutoJoinPolicy.TAB_AND_ORIGIN_SCOPED

    ) {

        // Check origin

        if (context.origin !== instance.contentContext?.origin) return false;

        // If tab-scoped, check context

        if (

            autoJoinPolicy === AutoJoinPolicy.TAB_AND_ORIGIN_SCOPED &&

            !isSameContext(context, instance.contentContext)

        )

            return false;


        return true;

    }


    return false;

}


interface AutoJoinTarget {

    session: CastSession;

    autoJoinContext: ContentContext;

}

function findAutoJoinTarget(instance: CastInstance) {

    for (const [, session] of activeSessions) {

        if (

            !session.sessionId ||

            session.appId !== instance.apiConfig?.sessionRequest.appId

        )

            continue;


        for (const context of session.autoJoinContexts) {

            if (isValidAutoJoinContext(instance, context)) {

                return { session, autoJoinContext: context } as AutoJoinTarget;

            }

        }

    }

}


/** Whitelist of safe message types from content. */

const allowedContentMessages: Array<Message["subject"]> = [

    "main:initializeCastSdk",

    "main:requestSession",

    "main:requestSessionById",

    "main:leaveSession",

    "bridge:sendCastReceiverMessage",

    "bridge:sendCastSessionMessage"

];


/** Chromecast base config to check compatibility with audio devices. */

let baseConfig: BaseConfig;

/** Shared receiver selector. */

let receiverSelector: Optional<ReceiverSelector>;


/** Set of active cast instances.  */

const activeInstances = new Set<CastInstance>();


/** Map of active session IDs to session info objects. */

const activeSessions = new Map<string, CastSession>();


/** Keeps track of cast API instances and provides bridge messaging. */

const castManager = new (class {

    async init() {

        // Handle incoming instance connections

        messaging.onConnect.addListener(async port => {

            if (port.name === "cast") {

                this.createInstance(port);

            } else if (port.name === "trusted-cast") {

                // Create trusted instance

                this.createInstance(port, undefined, true);

            }

        });


        // Pass receiver availability updates to cast API

        const updateReceiverAvailability = () => {

            const isAvailable = deviceManager.getDevices().length > 0;


            for (const instance of activeInstances) {

                instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                    subject: "cast:receiverAvailabilityUpdated",

                    data: { isAvailable }

                });

            }

        };


        deviceManager.addEventListener("deviceUp", updateReceiverAvailability);

        deviceManager.addEventListener(

            "deviceDown",

            updateReceiverAvailability

        );


        deviceManager.addEventListener("applicationClosed", ev => {

            const session = activeSessions.get(ev.detail.sessionId);

            if (!session?.sessionId) return;


            // Remove session from instances and notify SDK

            for (const instance of activeInstances) {

                if (instance.session === session) {

                    instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                        subject: "cast:sessionStopped",

                        data: { sessionId: session.sessionId }

                    });


                    delete instance.session;


                    if (instance.contentContext?.tabId) {

                        updateActionState(

                            ActionState.Default,

                            instance.contentContext.tabId

                        );

                    }

                }

            }


            activeSessions.delete(session.sessionId);

        });

    }


    /**

     * Finds a cast instance at the given tab (and optionally frame) ID.

     */

    getInstanceAt(tabId: number, frameId?: number) {

        for (const instance of activeInstances) {

            if (instance.contentContext?.tabId === tabId) {

                // If frame ID doesn't match go to next instance

                if (frameId && instance.contentContext.frameId !== frameId) {

                    continue;

                }


                return instance;

            }

        }

    }


    getInstanceByDeviceId(deviceId: string) {

        for (const instance of activeInstances) {

            if (instance.session?.deviceId === deviceId) return instance;

        }

    }


    /**

     * Creates a cast instance with a given port and connects messaging

     * correctly depending on the type of port.

     */

    async createInstance(

        port: AnyPort,

        contentContext?: ContentContext,

        isTrusted?: boolean

    ) {

        const instance = await (port instanceof MessagePort

            ? this.createInstanceFromBackground(port, contentContext)

            : this.createInstanceFromContent(port, isTrusted));


        activeInstances.add(instance);


        instance.contentPort.postMessage({

            subject: "cast:instanceCreated",

            data: { isAvailable: (await bridge.getInfo()).isVersionCompatible }

        });


        return instance;

    }


    /** Creates a cast instance with a `MessagePort` content port. */

    private async createInstanceFromBackground(

        contentPort: MessagePort,

        contentContext?: ContentContext

    ): Promise<CastInstance> {

        const instance = await createCastInstance({

            contentPort,

            contentContext,

            isTrusted: true

        });


        // Ensure only one instance per context

        if (contentContext) {

            for (const instance of activeInstances) {

                if (isSameContext(instance.contentContext, contentContext)) {

                    destroyCastInstance(instance);

                    break;

                }

            }

        }


        // cast instance -> (any)

        contentPort.addEventListener("message", ev => {

            handleContentMessage(instance, ev.data);

        });

        contentPort.start();


        return instance;

    }


    /**

     * Creates a cast instance with a WebExtension `Port` content port.

     */

    private async createInstanceFromContent(

        contentPort: Port,

        isTrusted?: boolean

    ): Promise<CastInstance> {

        if (

            contentPort.sender?.tab?.id === undefined ||

            contentPort.sender?.frameId === undefined

        ) {

            throw logger.error(

                "Cast instance created from content with an invalid port context."

            );

        }


        const instance = await createCastInstance({ contentPort, isTrusted });


        // cast instance -> (any)

        const onContentPortMessage = (message: Message) => {

            handleContentMessage(instance, message);

        };


        contentPort.onMessage.addListener(onContentPortMessage);

        contentPort.onDisconnect.addListener(() => {

            destroyCastInstance(instance);

        });


        return instance;

    }


    /**

     * Gets a receiver selection and loads the appropriate sender for a

     * given context.

     */

    async triggerCast(tabId: number, frameId = 0) {

        let selection: Nullable<ReceiverSelection>;

        try {

            selection = await getReceiverSelection({ tabId, frameId });

        } catch (err) {

            logger.error("Failed to get receiver selection (triggerCast)", err);

            return;

        }


        if (!selection) return;


        loadSender(selection, { tabId, frameId });

    }

})();


export default castManager;


/** Handles messages to cast instances from bridge. */

async function handleBridgeMessage(instance: CastInstance, message: Message) {

    // Intercept messages to store relevant info

    switch (message.subject) {

        case "main:castSessionCreated": {

            // Close after session is created

            if (

                receiverSelector?.isOpen &&

                // If selector context is the same as the instance context

                isSameContext(

                    receiverSelector.pageInfo,

                    instance.contentContext

                ) &&

                // If selector is supposed to close

                (await options.get("receiverSelectorWaitForConnection"))

            ) {

                receiverSelector.close();

            }


            const { receiverId: deviceId } = message.data;


            if (!instance.session) {

                logger.error("Instance is missing session!");

                break;

            }


            instance.session.sessionId = message.data.sessionId;

            activeSessions.set(message.data.sessionId, instance.session);


            const device = deviceManager.getDeviceById(deviceId);

            if (!device) {

                logger.error(

                    "[on main:castSessionCreated]: Could not find device with ID:",

                    deviceId

                );

                break;

            }


            instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                subject: "cast:sessionCreated",

                data: {

                    ...message.data,

                    receiver: createReceiver(device)

                }

            });


            if (instance.contentContext?.tabId) {

                updateActionState(

                    ActionState.Connected,

                    instance.contentContext?.tabId

                );

            }


            break;

        }


        case "main:castSessionUpdated":

            instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                subject: "cast:sessionUpdated",

                data: message.data

            });

    }


    instance.contentPort.postMessage(message);

}


/**

 * Handle content messages from the cast instance. These will either

 * be handled here in the background script or forwarded to the

 * bridge associated with the cast instance.

 */

async function handleContentMessage(instance: CastInstance, message: Message) {

    // Limit untrusted instances to allowed messages subset

    if (

        !allowedContentMessages.includes(message.subject) &&

        !instance.isTrusted

    ) {

        logger.error(`Forbidden message type! (${message.subject})`);

        destroyCastInstance(instance);

        return;

    }


    const [destination] = message.subject.split(":");

    if (destination === "bridge") {

        instance.session?.bridgePort.postMessage(message);

    }


    switch (message.subject) {

        case "main:initializeCastSdk": {

            instance.apiConfig = message.data.apiConfig;

            instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                subject: "cast:receiverAvailabilityUpdated",

                data: {

                    isAvailable: deviceManager.getDevices().length > 0

                }

            });


            // No need to check for existing sessions if page-scoped

            if (

                instance.apiConfig.autoJoinPolicy === AutoJoinPolicy.PAGE_SCOPED

            ) {

                break;

            }


            // Check existing sessions for a valid auto join target

            const target = findAutoJoinTarget(instance);

            if (target) joinSession(instance, target.session);


            break;

        }


        // User has triggered receiver selection via the cast API

        case "main:requestSession": {

            const { sessionRequest, receiverDevice } = message.data;


            // Handle trusted instance receiver selection bypass

            if (receiverDevice) {

                if (receiverSelector?.isOpen && instance.contentContext) {

                    receiverSelector.pageInfo = {

                        ...instance.contentContext,

                        url: (

                            await browser.webNavigation.getFrame({

                                tabId: instance.contentContext?.tabId,

                                frameId: instance.contentContext?.frameId

                            })

                        ).url

                    };

                }


                if (!instance.isTrusted) {

                    logger.error(

                        "Cast instance not trusted to bypass receiver selection!"

                    );

                    destroyCastInstance(instance);

                    break;

                }


                const session = await createCastSession({

                    instance,

                    deviceId: receiverDevice.id,

                    appId: sessionRequest.appId

                });


                session.bridgePort.postMessage({

                    subject: "bridge:createCastSession",

                    data: {

                        appId: sessionRequest.appId,

                        receiverDevice

                    }

                });


                break;

            }


            try {

                const selection = await getReceiverSelection({

                    castInstance: instance

                });


                // Handle cancellation

                if (!selection) {

                    instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                        subject: "cast:sessionRequestCancelled"

                    });


                    break;

                }


                /**

                 * If the media type returned from the selector has

                 * been changed, we need to cancel the current

                 * sender and switch it out for the right one.

                 */

                if (selection.mediaType !== ReceiverSelectorMediaType.App) {

                    instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                        subject: "cast:sessionRequestCancelled"

                    });


                    if (!instance.contentContext) {

                        throw logger.error("Missing content context");

                    }

                    loadSender(selection, instance.contentContext);


                    break;

                }


                instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                    subject: "cast:receiverAction",

                    data: {

                        receiver: createReceiver(selection.device),

                        action: ReceiverAction.CAST

                    }

                });


                const session = await createCastSession({

                    instance,

                    deviceId: selection.device.id,

                    appId: sessionRequest.appId

                });


                session.bridgePort.postMessage({

                    subject: "bridge:createCastSession",

                    data: {

                        appId: sessionRequest.appId,

                        receiverDevice: selection.device

                    }

                });

            } catch (err) {

                // TODO: Report errors properly

                instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                    subject: "cast:sessionRequestCancelled"

                });

            }


            break;

        }


        case "main:requestSessionById": {

            const session = activeSessions.get(message.data.sessionId);

            if (!session) {

                logger.log(

                    `Session not found! (id: ${message.data.sessionId})`

                );

                break;

            }


            if (instance.apiConfig?.sessionRequest.appId === session.appId) {

                joinSession(instance, session);


                // If requesting by ID, add to the list of auto join contexts

                if (instance.contentContext) {

                    session.autoJoinContexts.add(instance.contentContext);

                }

            }


            break;

        }


        case "main:leaveSession": {

            if (!instance.contentContext || !instance.session?.sessionId) {

                logger.error("Cannot leave session, instance invalid!");

                break;

            }


            // Find auto join target for this instance

            const target = findAutoJoinTarget(instance);

            if (target) {

                // Remove auto join context for future instances

                instance.session.autoJoinContexts.delete(

                    target.autoJoinContext

                );


                const sessionAppId = instance.session.appId;

                leaveSession(instance);


                /**

                 * Disconnect other instances within the scope of this

                 * instances's auto join policy.

                 */

                for (const activeInstance of activeInstances) {

                    if (

                        (activeInstance === instance ||

                            activeInstance.session?.appId) !== sessionAppId

                    )

                        continue;


                    if (

                        isValidAutoJoinContext(

                            activeInstance,

                            target.autoJoinContext

                        )

                    ) {

                        leaveSession(activeInstance);

                    }

                }

            } else {

                leaveSession(instance);

            }

        }

    }

}


/**

 * Loads the appropriate sender for a given receiver selector response.

 */

async function loadSender(

    selection: ReceiverSelection,

    contentContext: ContentContext

) {

    // Cancelled

    if (!selection) {

        return;

    }


    switch (selection.mediaType) {

        case ReceiverSelectorMediaType.App: {

            const instance = castManager.getInstanceAt(

                contentContext.tabId,

                contentContext.frameId

            );

            if (!instance) {

                throw logger.error(

                    `Cast instance not found at tabId ${contentContext.tabId} / frameId ${contentContext.frameId}`

                );

            }


            if (!instance.apiConfig?.sessionRequest.appId) {

                throw logger.error("Invalid session request");

            }


            instance.contentPort.postMessage({

                subject: "cast:receiverAction",

                data: {

                    receiver: createReceiver(selection.device),

                    action: ReceiverAction.CAST

                }

            });


            const session = await createCastSession({

                instance,

                deviceId: selection.device.id

            });

The files you provided for action.ts, background.ts, and castManager.ts provide a very clear picture of why your "Cast" button is failing to launch.
The Core Problem: A "Silent" CSP Block

The error in your logs (‘script-src’ directive contains a forbidden 'unsafe-eval' keyword) is not just a warning; it is a kill switch. When Firefox loads your extension, it checks the manifest.json. Because you have not defined a content_security_policy in your manifest.json, Firefox defaults to the strictest possible policy for MV3. When your UI (likely your Popup.svelte or the injected ReceiverSelector) tries to run, the Svelte compiler or the framework itself attempts to use dynamic script evaluation.

Firefox blocks this execution before it even reaches your click-handlers. That is why you see zero output in the Wiretap log—the bridge:launchApp command is never even sent because the code triggering it is blocked by the browser's security layer.
The Fix

You have two paths to resolve this. Choose the one that fits your development flow:
Option 1: The "Production-Ready" Fix (Recommended)

You need to force your bundler (Vite, Rollup, or Webpack) to stop generating code that relies on eval() or dynamic string-to-code execution.

    Locate your build configuration (e.g., vite.config.ts, rollup.config.js).

    If using the @sveltejs/vite-plugin-svelte plugin, ensure you are not using the runtime compiler (compilerOptions: { generate: 'dom' }). You should be using the pre-compiled version.

    Once the code is "safe," add the policy to your manifest.json to tell Firefox it's okay to run:

JSON

"content_security_policy": {
  "extension_pages": "script-src 'self'; object-src 'self';"
}

Option 2: The "Development" Quick Fix (To verify functionality)

If you just want to get it working now to verify the bridge, you can downgrade the Manifest Version temporarily to MV2, which has much looser security defaults.

    Change "manifest_version": 3 to "manifest_version": 2 in your manifest.json.

    Remove the action block and replace it with browser_action.

    Add "content_security_policy": "script-src 'self' 'unsafe-eval'; object-src 'self'" to your manifest.json.

A Critical Observation

In the src/background/castManager.ts file you sent, the code is truncated at the end of the loadSender function.

                instance,
                deviceId: selection.device.id
            });

            s // <-- The file cuts off right here

If your build has this file cut off, it will never trigger the cast. Make sure your src/background/castManager.ts has the full logic, specifically the session.bridgePort.postMessage({ subject: "bridge:createCastSession" ... }) call.
Next Step

If you are using a popup, please open src/ui/popup/Popup.svelte. Look for the code that triggers the cast (likely a button with an on:click handler). Does it send a message like browser.runtime.sendMessage?

i want to be able to execute find commands like this "└─$ find src/ -type f \( -name "*.ts" -o -name "*.svelte" \) -exec echo -e "\n\n--- FILE: {} ---" \; -exec cat {}" I dont get the `\),\(`, `\;` after the first exec, and the last exec

The reason find syntax looks so "messy" is that you are interacting with two systems at once: the Shell (Bash/Zsh) and the find command itself.

Characters like (, ), and ; have special meanings to the Shell (e.g., ; tells the shell to run a new command). Therefore, you must "escape" them with a backslash (\) so they are passed to the find command literally.

Here is the breakdown of the specific parts you asked about:
1. The Grouping: \( ... \)

Without the parentheses, find processes conditions in a linear "AND" chain.

    Your command: -name "*.ts" -o -name "*.svelte"

    Without \( \): find would interpret this as: "Find files that end in .ts OR find any file if it ends in .svelte." This usually results in unintended behavior.

    With \( \): You are telling find: "Treat this specific logic (A or B) as a single block." It forces find to evaluate the OR condition first, then apply that to the rest of the search.

Why the backslash?
Because if you typed ( ) without the \, your terminal would try to execute a subshell command instead of letting find see the parentheses.
2. The Execution: -exec ... \;

The -exec flag is how find runs commands on the files it locates. It follows a strict syntax:
find [path] -exec [command] {} \;

    {}: This is a placeholder. find replaces this automatically with the path of every file it matches.

    ; (The Semicolon): This tells find that the command is finished. It acts like a "period" at the end of a sentence.

    \;: Because the semicolon is a special character in the shell, you must escape it so find receives it, not your terminal.

3. The Multiple -exec (Chaining)

find is powerful because it doesn't just stop at one action. You can perform multiple actions in sequence for every file found.

    First -exec: Runs echo .... This prints the "header" (the file name).

    Second -exec: Runs cat {}. This reads the file content.

A Critical Correction

In the command you provided, you are missing the final \;.

Your command:
... -exec cat {}

If you run this, it will fail with an error like: find: missing argument to -exec.

The correct final structure is:
Bash

find src/ -type f \( -name "*.ts" -o -name "*.svelte" \) -exec echo -e "\n\n--- FILE: {} ---" \; -exec cat {} \;

Summary of the "Symbols"
Symbol	Purpose	Why the backslash?
\(	Start a logical group	Terminal uses ( for subshells.
\)	End a logical group	Terminal uses ) for subshells.
\;	Finish the -exec command	Terminal uses ; to chain commands.

Think of it as a logical pipeline: Find (files) -> Filter (grouping) -> Action 1 (Header) -> Action 2 (Content).

manpages for the find command

To access the official manual for find on your machine, simply open your terminal and type:
Bash

man find

How to navigate a manpage

Manpages are displayed using a pager (usually less). Here are the essential keys to help you navigate:

    Arrow Keys: Scroll up and down.

    / (Forward Slash): Follow this with a keyword to search (e.g., /exec and press Enter to jump to the exec section).

    n: Jump to the next occurrence of your search term.

    q: Quit and return to the terminal.

Understanding the Structure

The find manpage is dense because the tool is incredibly powerful. To learn it effectively, focus on these four core sections, which are always presented in the same order in the documentation:

    SYNOPSIS: This is the "blueprint." It shows you that the command is structured as find [path] [expression].

    DESCRIPTION: Explains the flow. It tells you that find works by evaluating a series of "tests" (expressions) against every file it encounters.

    TESTS / PRIMARY: This is the longest section. It lists the filters you can apply, such as -name, -type, -mtime (time modified), and -size.

    ACTIONS: This lists the things find can do to the files it found, such as -delete, -print, and your familiar -exec.

Why the Manpage is Confusing (and how to hack it)

The reason you were confused by the syntax (the \( \), \;) is that the find manpage defines these as Operators.

When you search for the word "OPERATORS" in the manpage, you will see a section describing how to group logic. It explains that -o is an "OR" operator and that parentheses are used to override the default "AND" precedence.
Better Alternatives for Learning

If the standard man page feels like reading a legal document, here are three ways to get the same information faster:

    TLDR: Many users install the tldr tool. If you have it, run tldr find. It gives you the "Too Long; Didn't Read" version with 5–10 practical examples.

    man -k: If you can't remember the exact name of a command or want to see related commands, use man -k find (this searches the short descriptions of all manpages).

    Online Documentation: If you prefer a web-based view (which is much easier to read than the terminal), search for man7.org find. It is the canonical source for the Linux manual pages and is much easier to navigate via your browser's "Find" (Ctrl+F) feature.

Pro-tip: When reading the manpage, always look at the EXAMPLES section (if available). The find manpage is often dry, but the examples show exactly how the escaping (like \;) is applied in real-world scenarios.

--- FILE: src/background/action.ts ---
import logger from "../lib/logger";
import castManager from "./castManager";

const _ = browser.i18n.getMessage;

const ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_DARK = "icons/cast-default-dark.svg";
const ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_LIGHT = "icons/cast-default-light.svg";
const ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_DARK = "icons/cast-connecting-dark.svg";
const ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_LIGHT = "icons/cast-connecting-light.svg";
const ACTION_ICON_CONNECTED = "icons/cast-connected.svg";

const isDarkTheme = window.matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)").matches;

export enum ActionState {
    Default,
    Connecting,
    Connected
}

/** Updates action details depending on given state. */
export function updateActionState(state: ActionState, tabId?: number) {
    let title: string;
    let path = isDarkTheme
        ? ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_LIGHT
        : ACTION_ICON_DEFAULT_DARK;

    switch (state) {
        case ActionState.Default:
            title = _("actionTitleDefault");
            break;
        case ActionState.Connecting:
            title = _("actionTitleConnecting");
            path = isDarkTheme
                ? ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_LIGHT
                : ACTION_ICON_CONNECTING_DARK;
            break;
        case ActionState.Connected:
            title = _("actionTitleConnected");
            path = ACTION_ICON_CONNECTED;
            break;
    }

    browser.action.setTitle({ tabId, title });
    browser.action.setIcon({ tabId, path });
}

export function initAction() {
    logger.info("init (action)");

    updateActionState(ActionState.Default);

    browser.action.onClicked.addListener(async tab => {
        if (tab.id === undefined) {
            logger.error("Tab ID not found in browser action handler.");
            return;
        }

        castManager.triggerCast(tab.id);
    });
}


--- FILE: src/background/background.ts ---
import logger from "../lib/logger";
import options from "../lib/options";
import bridge, { type BridgeInfo } from "../lib/bridge";
import { baseConfigStorage, fetchBaseConfig } from "../lib/chromecastConfigApi";

import defaultOptions from "../defaultOptions";
import messaging from "../messaging";

import castManager from "./castManager";
import deviceManager from "./deviceManager";

import { initAction } from "./action";
import { initMenus } from "./menus";
import { initWhitelist } from "./whitelist";
import { cacheUaInfo, getChromeUserAgentString } from "../lib/userAgents";

const _ = browser.i18n.getMessage;

/**
 * On install, set the default options before initializing the
 * extension. On update, handle any unset values and set to the new
 * defaults.
 */
browser.runtime.onInstalled.addListener(async details => {
    switch (details.reason) {
        case "install": {
            // Set defaults
            await options.setAll(defaultOptions);

            // Extension initialization
            init();
            break;
        }

        case "update": {
            // Set new defaults
            await options.update(defaultOptions);
            break;
        }
    }
});

/**
 * Checks whether the bridge can be reached and is compatible with the
 * current version of the extension. If not, triggers a notification
 * with the appropriate info.
 */
async function notifyBridgeCompat() {
    logger.info("checking for bridge...");

    let info: BridgeInfo;
    try {
        info = await bridge.getInfo();
    } catch (err) {
        logger.info("... bridge issue!");
        return;
    }

    if (info.isVersionCompatible) {
        logger.info("... bridge compatible!");
    } else {
        logger.info("... bridge incompatible!");

        const updateNotificationId = await browser.notifications.create({
            type: "basic",
            title: `${_("extensionName")} — ${_(
                "optionsBridgeIssueStatusTitle"
            )}`,
            message: info.isVersionOlder
                ? _("optionsBridgeOlderAction")
                : _("optionsBridgeNewerAction")
        });

        browser.notifications.onClicked.addListener(notificationId => {
            if (notificationId !== updateNotificationId) {
                return;
            }

            browser.tabs.create({
                url: `https://github.com/hensm/fx_cast/releases/tag/v${info.expectedVersion}`
            });
        });
    }
}

/**
 * Updates locally-stored base config data if never downloaded or since
 * expired.
 */
async function cacheBaseConfig() {
    const { baseConfigUpdated } = await baseConfigStorage.get(
        "baseConfigUpdated"
    );

    // If never updated or updated more than 48 hours ago
    if (
        !baseConfigUpdated ||
        (Date.now() - baseConfigUpdated) / 1000 >= 172800
    ) {
        logger.info("Fetching updated Chromecast base config...");
        const baseConfig = await fetchBaseConfig();
        if (baseConfig) {
            await baseConfigStorage.set({
                baseConfig,
                baseConfigUpdated: Date.now()
            });
        }
    }
}

let isInitialized = false;

async function init() {
    if (isInitialized) {
        return;
    }

    /**
     * If options haven't been set yet, we can't properly initialize,
     * so wait until init is called again in the onInstalled listener.
     */
    if (!(await options.getAll())) {
        return;
    }

    logger.info("init");
    isInitialized = true;

    await notifyBridgeCompat();

    await deviceManager.init();
    await castManager.init();

    await initAction();
    await initMenus();
    await initWhitelist();

    messaging.onMessage.addListener(message => {
        switch (message.subject) {
            case "main:refreshDeviceManager":
                deviceManager.refresh();
                break;
        }
    });
}

cacheUaInfo();
cacheBaseConfig();
init();


--- FILE: src/background/castManager.ts ---
import bridge from "../lib/bridge";
import {
    type BaseConfig,
    baseConfigStorage,
    getAppTag
} from "../lib/chromecastConfigApi";
import logger from "../lib/logger";
import messaging, { type Message, type Port } from "../messaging";
import options from "../lib/options";
import type { TypedMessagePort } from "../lib/TypedMessagePort";

import {
    type ReceiverDevice,
    type ReceiverSelectorAppInfo,
    ReceiverSelectorMediaType,
    type ReceiverSelectorPageInfo
} from "../types";

import type { ApiConfig } from "../cast/sdk/classes";
import { AutoJoinPolicy, ReceiverAction } from "../cast/sdk/enums";
import { createReceiver } from "../cast/utils";

import ReceiverSelector, {
    type ReceiverSelection,
    type ReceiverSelectorMediaMessage,
    type ReceiverSelectorReceiverMessage
} from "./receiverSelector";

import deviceManager from "./deviceManager";
import { ActionState, updateActionState } from "./action";

type AnyPort = Port | TypedMessagePort<Message>;

export interface ContentContext {
    tabId: number;
    frameId: number;
    origin?: string;
}

/** Checks if two content contexts match. */
function isSameContext(ctx1?: ContentContext, ctx2?: ContentContext) {
    if (!ctx1 || !ctx2) return false;
    return ctx1?.tabId === ctx2?.tabId && ctx1?.frameId === ctx2?.frameId;
}

interface CastSession {
    bridgePort: Port;
    deviceId: string;
    appId: string;
    sessionId?: string;
    autoJoinContexts: Set<ContentContext>;
}

/** Creates a cast session object and sets up messaging. */
async function createCastSession(opts: {
    deviceId: string;
    instance: CastInstance;
    appId?: string;
}) {
    // If not explicitly provided, use session request app ID
    if (!opts.appId) {
        if (!opts.instance.apiConfig?.sessionRequest) {
            throw logger.error(
                "App ID not provided and instance missing valid session request!"
            );
        }
        opts.appId = opts.instance.apiConfig.sessionRequest.appId;
    }

    const session: CastSession = {
        bridgePort: await bridge.connect(),
        deviceId: opts.deviceId,
        appId: opts.appId,
        autoJoinContexts: new Set()
    };

    if (opts.instance.contentContext) {
        session.autoJoinContexts.add(opts.instance.contentContext);
    }

    opts.instance.session = session;
    opts.instance.bridgeMessageListener = message => {
